  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_24cdb264-5612-49b2-8597-ea7ce7a9669c'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9120545274131060943"><b>Nalini Singh pulls away another dark layer of sheer desire, revealing passions unknown, in her latest novel about the world of the Psy. A ghost returns from a leopard changeling’s past, making him question everything—even his base animal instincts…</b><br/><br/>Clay Bennett is a powerful DarkRiver sentinel, but he grew up in the slums with his human mother, never knowing his changeling </span>
  <span id="freeText9120545274131060943" style="display:none"><b>Nalini Singh pulls away another dark layer of sheer desire, revealing passions unknown, in her latest novel about the world of the Psy. A ghost returns from a leopard changeling’s past, making him question everything—even his base animal instincts…</b><br /><br />Clay Bennett is a powerful DarkRiver sentinel, but he grew up in the slums with his human mother, never knowing his changeling father. As a young boy without the bonds of Pack, he tried to stifle his animal nature. He failed…and committed the most extreme act of violence, killing a man and losing his best friend, Talin, in the bloody aftermath. Everything good in him died the day he was told that she, too, was dead.<br /><br />Talin McKade barely survived a childhood drenched in bloodshed and terror. Now a new nightmare is stalking her life–the street children she works to protect are disappearing and turning up dead. Determined to keep them safe, she unlocks the darkest secret in her heart and returns to ask the help of the strongest man she knows…<br /><br />Clay lost Talin once. He will not let her go again, his hunger to possess her, a clawing need born of the leopard within. As they race to save the innocent, Clay and Talin must face the violent truths of their past…or lose everything that ever mattered.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9120545274131060943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7928789957902888664">3.5<br/><br/>This book was just slightly better than okay for me. I didn't really care for Clay or Talin. So their relationship was just ok for me. I did enjoy the plot and everything else it was just the couple that was meh. </span>

<div id="review_2419250136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2419250136" />
    <a title="Sophia Triad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44642860-sophia-triad"><img alt="Sophia Triad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591419108p2/44642860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419250136?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia Triad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia Triad" href="/user/show/44642860-sophia-triad">Sophia Triad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=experiments">experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=1paranormal-lovestories">1paranormal-lovestories</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419250136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17531428974853180768"><b>Clay Bennett (Changeling) and Talin McKade (Human)</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“Talin,” he said softly, surrendering completely to the madness. <br/>Her spine stiffened, but at last, she turned. <br/>And the entire world stopped breathing.</b>
</i><br/><br/>After the out-of-this-world Psy and the larger-than-life Changelings, in this book we meet...well...the average, boring, helpless, weak...humans.<br/><br/>Talin the human and Clay the leopard belonged to each other since they were children. <br/><br/>Clay realised that soon. So, when Talin was in trouble, he did no</span>
  <span id="freeText17531428974853180768" style="display:none"><b>Clay Bennett (Changeling) and Talin McKade (Human)</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Talin,” he said softly, surrendering completely to the madness. <br />Her spine stiffened, but at last, she turned. <br />And the entire world stopped breathing.</b>
</i><br /><br />After the out-of-this-world Psy and the larger-than-life Changelings, in this book we meet...well...the average, boring, helpless, weak...humans.<br /><br />Talin the human and Clay the leopard belonged to each other since they were children. <br /><br />Clay realised that soon. So, when Talin was in trouble, he did not hesitate to kill for her and as a result he was locked away for years.<br />Talin, on the other hand, did not want to accept that she belonged to Clay. So, when Clay asked for her, he was informed that she died.<br /><br />Nowadays, Clay is a powerful sentinel in DarkRiver pack. He has never overcome the lose of Talin and for this reason he has been always on the verge of being lost in his animal side.<br />Talin has grown up and has never stopped thinking of Clay – although she has never tried to find him and explained to him why she pretended that she was dead. But now she is in trouble. She is a social worker and her children disappear and die horribly. Only Clay can help her.<br /><br />When Clay sees Talin again, he is absolutely sure that he will never let her go again. <br />Unfortunately a) Talin is sick and b) someone wants her dead.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You’re mine. Therefore you’re perfect.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I loved this book, not so much for the love story but mostly for the horrific side story of the missing children. I really wanted the children to survive, I was wondering for the reasons they were abducted and the reasons for the experiments. <br />I was satisfied with the answers and the solutions, but I think the way Talin's sickness was handled, it was a bit farfetched.<br /><br />More interesting characters are introduced and basically this book is an introduction to the next book: Hostage to Pleasure.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17531428974853180768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11648817812512371355"><b>Full review finally posted on 11/3/13</b><br/><br/><b>5…Fantastic...Stars!!! </b><br/><br/>I was shocked at how much I LOVED this somewhat heartbreaking, humorous, endearing, and amazingly heartwarming story. This book's focus was about the main couple's complicated and enduring relationship rather than the world-building aspect of the over all story arc. <br/><br/>I won't lie, I struggled at first with the heroine and what seemed to be her weak behavior; however, once I realized why she reacted the way she did, I ended up her biggest </span>
  <span id="freeText11648817812512371355" style="display:none"><b>Full review finally posted on 11/3/13</b><br /><br /><b>5…Fantastic...Stars!!! </b><br /><br />I was shocked at how much I LOVED this somewhat heartbreaking, humorous, endearing, and amazingly heartwarming story. This book's focus was about the main couple's complicated and enduring relationship rather than the world-building aspect of the over all story arc. <br /><br />I won't lie, I struggled at first with the heroine and what seemed to be her weak behavior; however, once I realized why she reacted the way she did, I ended up her biggest cheerleader. I quickly came to realized because of all she'd been through, that Tally, a <i>human</i>, is emotionally the strongest heroine in this series thus far, and I loved her all the more for all she's been through. Her and Clay's tragic yet inspiring love story was simply phenomenal. My only grumble was how cruel and demeaning the hero was toward the heroine at the beginning of the story. Other than that, I loved this book. <br /><br />It's been over a month since I read this story and I'm still thinking about it. If that doesn't deserve 5 stars, I don't know what does. <br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_582978315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/582978315" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582978315?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8486069-mine-to-possess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=review-books-done">review-books-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=aoc">aoc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582978315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15758370709582511783">August 2016 re-read: Over the years since I've first read this book I've had many feelings about it. Some good, some ... well, not so good. For a long time this was my least favorite book - and I don't think it'll ever be one of my favorites. It's too ... uneasy, and hits an incredibly uncomfortable spot for me. But I have reached a new understanding with this book, and the characters that take the spotlight in it.<br/><br/>My biggest problem was always Talin. She had an incredibly hard childhood, filled </span>
  <span id="freeText15758370709582511783" style="display:none">August 2016 re-read: Over the years since I've first read this book I've had many feelings about it. Some good, some ... well, not so good. For a long time this was my least favorite book - and I don't think it'll ever be one of my favorites. It's too ... uneasy, and hits an incredibly uncomfortable spot for me. But I have reached a new understanding with this book, and the characters that take the spotlight in it.<br><br>My biggest problem was always Talin. She had an incredibly hard childhood, filled with abuse - of many and varied kinds - and then, when she was barely old enough for school, she witnessed the very horrific death of her abuser at the hands of her best friend: Clay. Clay is Changeling, so you can imagine that it was messy and gory, and not at all something that is easily brushed past. I don't blame Clay for that. And Talin doesn't either. But it's still more trauma on top of the trauma she'd already been subjected to day in and day out.<br><br>I used to be irritated with Talin. Everything Clay did was for his love of her. His care and need to care for her. Why did she treat him with such callous disregard? Why did she disappear from his life, letting him think she was dead, for so long? Why cause him that pain? Honestly, I hated Talin for a long, long, long time.<br><br>Something new happened on this read though - and this is one of the reasons I love re-reading so much - I understand Talin now. She did what she had to do in order to survive. She'd been traumatized, lost, left, and forgotten. She was a <em>child</em>. And Clay, though he was only a few years older than Talin, was already growing into the personality that would one day lead to his being a Sentinel. The power differential between them was so great, and the pain that Talin couldn't forget was a barrier.<br><br>Talin needed to heal herself, become a whole person again, before being dragged under someone's strong personality. Clay wouldn't have done it intentionally, wouldn't have wanted to damage her - he loved her - but when someone is broken, it's hard to not subjugate yourself to a much stronger personality. It's hard to not become the person they, however subtly or unintentionally, push you to being.<br><br>So Talin took that time. And I get that. I <strong>finally</strong> understand that. I don't know if it's me growing, or if I just finally read what was always there....I don't know why I understand this now when I never did before, but I do. I also get the blame, and the hurt, the pain and the worry about being abandoned again. How could she feel any differently? I was still, <em>slightly</em>, annoyed by the fact that she basically laid claim to Clay, becoming possessive of him even with his Pack, when she didn't really trust him. But feelings are nuanced. A person can feel many things for one person or situation at a time. Just because there were doubts doesn't mean she didn't already love him.<br><br>What really surprised me this time was the anger I felt towards Clay. Talin, like many sexual abuse survivors, took to hurting herself with sex. I understand this in ways that I wish I didn't. When Talin lashed out at Clay that she'd 'been with so many men she couldn't remember all their names or faces' he became angry. Rage-filled anger. Not physically directed at Talin, but emotionally he became distant until she pushed him again to address it. His anger quickly became about the fact that she should have kept herself safe and cherished, but - initially - it was possessive. She was his and no one else should have had her.<br><br>Even if she'd never been abused. Even if there was never that trauma. She could have slept with whomever she so desired in her past. Like he did. <strong>Like he did</strong>. Argh!!<br><br>Look, I get it. This is the flip side of the Changeling possessiveness. He always knew she was <em>his</em>. But she didn't, and she was hurt - hurt beyond measure. For him to judge her....it enrages me.<br><br>In the end, Clay and Talin work through everything in their past and present to become a strong united couple. I feel confident in them, and their future. And while I don't love everything they did to each other, how much they hurt each other, I finally have a new appreciation for the choices each of them made, and can look at them without the level of irritation I carried before.<br><br>Review also posted at <a href="https://thebookeaters.net/2016/08/29/review-mine-to-possess/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Eaters</a><br><br><br><br><b>Original Thoughts</b><br>Talin irritates the hell out of me. If she hadn't spent the majority of the book <i>afraid</i> of Clay, I probably wouldn't have such an issue with her. But, as a friend of mine said, she comes off as a snot.<br><br>Thanks Anna for sharing this with me, it's perfect for Talin ;)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379796230i/615958.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Their history with each other is fantastic, and full of depth. It really shows how Clay became the person he is. And I loved seeing more about this intensely shut off character. <br><br>To be fair, their history shows why Talin became the person she did as well. I could understand her issues with Clay for a good part of the book, but it just went a little too far for me. That's personal and may be different for other people that read.<br><br>The reason that Talin seeks Clay out - the "mystery" of the book, was really interesting, too. It moves things along in the overall storyline very nicely.<br><br>Overall, I enjoy this book, but it's mostly for Clay and the world implications. Talin just pisses me off.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15758370709582511783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1685535910?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2016</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1685535910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4934560233397616290"><b>*** 4 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with my family at BB&B!</b><br/><br/>This is the fourth book in the series and I keep enjoying as much as when I started!!! It is a PNR with a new couple finding love in each book. The best part of the series, at least to me, is the amazing world building and the specifics which make up the differences between the three main races - the Psy, the Changelings (or animal shifters), and humans. In all the previous books we got to meet Psy and Changeling characters, letting us into the world </span>
  <span id="freeText4934560233397616290" style="display:none"><b>*** 4 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with my family at BB&amp;B!</b><br /><br />This is the fourth book in the series and I keep enjoying as much as when I started!!! It is a PNR with a new couple finding love in each book. The best part of the series, at least to me, is the amazing world building and the specifics which make up the differences between the three main races - the Psy, the Changelings (or animal shifters), and humans. In all the previous books we got to meet Psy and Changeling characters, letting us into the world of brain dominance and physical prowess, but we only heard of the humans, a bit like a filler for the background...<br /><br />This time, our Leopard Changeling Clay is faced with a ghost from his past. Tally was the 8 year old human girl for whose safety he committed a murder and spend his youth in juvenile detention.... When he came out, he was told she is dead and he never truly stopped grieving for her... Now she is a woman, beautiful and alive, who has come to him to seek help. She has become a social worker and the kids who have been associated with the foundation she is working for, are disappearing, some of them found soon after disfigured, butchered, and lifeless... She wants to save the last one of them, a kid she cares for deeply... Her need of the over protective Leopard is greater than the shame and guilt she feels over lying to him .... But would Clay be able to put away the pain and hurt in order to help her? And could she hope that he could even forgive her??? <br /><br />Clay, however, is a hard sell, and the nature of his beast is not very forgiving... The enigmatic cat is going to have his pound of flesh!!!<br /><br />I liked Clay a lot and had some issues with the unnecessary angst Tally liked to wallow in... What I loved were the cameos by the previous couples and seeing them grow into devoted lovers and strong players in the world's powers system. The little Cubs are adorable and I want to adopt them all!!! The Psy Council is still fascinating and the machinations behind the scene are intricate and engaging... After finishing this book I wanted to dive straight into the next one, but I had to remind myself to pace the good stuff and not to gorge on treats, which in my case means fun books:-)<br /><br />I would recommend this series to lovers of romance and a setting of a world full of Fantasy and magnetic creatures! It is a pure pleasure meeting all the characters NS creates for us!!! <br /><br />I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find pleasure in every book!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4934560233397616290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87708169" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87708169" />
    <a title="Beanbag Love" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love"><img alt="Beanbag Love" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249531311p2/2598237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87708169?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beanbag Love" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beanbag Love" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love">Beanbag Love</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87708169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17509582950272466466">This installment of Singh's Psy-Changeling series was different in that neither of the two leads was a psy. I have to admit, I prefer that. The psy storyline always seems the same to me. We have to go through the whole 'awakening' thing and it always seems to present the same way. So this was a refreshing change and I liked the plot and story better.<br/><br/>However, the writing itself was weaker than the others. Singh reused several phrases to the point were I actually laughed a couple of times. "His le</span>
  <span id="freeText17509582950272466466" style="display:none">This installment of Singh's Psy-Changeling series was different in that neither of the two leads was a psy. I have to admit, I prefer that. The psy storyline always seems the same to me. We have to go through the whole 'awakening' thing and it always seems to present the same way. So this was a refreshing change and I liked the plot and story better.<br /><br />However, the writing itself was weaker than the others. Singh reused several phrases to the point were I actually laughed a couple of times. "His leopard stilled" or "he stilled" or "he went leopard still" could have been a drinking game. I got this picture of a guy who would freeze in mid-conversation and it was actually pretty comical when of course it wasn't meant to be.<br /><br />Then there were the inner arguments for Talin. "I love him but he can't love me but it will kill him if something happens to me but is he only with me for loyalty? No, damnit, he cares!" and on and on and on. Really it felt more like padding. <br /><br />The mystery and the story itself was very good though. And I really liked the romance (even with the repetitive phrases and inner monologues). At first it seemed a bit squicky because he sees a woman with his childhood friend's scent and appearance, but thinks his friend is dead. The last time he saw her she was eight. But his first thoughts about this mystery woman are sexual. Huh? Doesn't add up for me.<br /><br />Thankfully we move on from there and it doesn't feel squicky anymore because we forget that little tidbit, but it would have been nice if his first reaction had been a bit more chaste.<br /><br />Clay and Talin were friends in a low income apartment complex. She was an abused foster child and he was a changeling living with his crazy human mother who demanded he suppress his leopard half. He's older than Talin by about five years. They meet when she's three and helps him after he's gotten hurt outside and nobody bothers to notice. She's not afraid of him and he immediately becomes her best friend and protector. Until he goes too far with the latter and they're cruelly separated just when they need each other the most.<br /><br />There are several things that make this a really nice setup. One, they pretty much bonded as children without the romantic side to it. Two, they were separated by tragedy and violence that served to not only mark their destinies, but to bring them back together. Three, they haven't seen each other since childhood and so are getting to know one another while continuing to have this base of knowledge (regarding their past traumas) but also a store of good memories to draw from. It's a nice mix. <br /><br />There's murder and mayhem and bad things happen to kids. Nothing with the kids is too graphic, but you are in no doubt about it's existence. Justice is served and the next book is set up nicely.<br /><br />So far, all the Psy-Changeling books have gotten four stars from me. I have criticism of all of them, but they're all good solid reads. <br /><br />(edited for clarity)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17509582950272466466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14297348611996077394">On the one hand, I like the world that is building in these books. It is extremely intriguing and different.<br/><br/>On the other hand, I didn't particularly like the female love interest in this book - Tally. She was a victim of childhood abuse, and that was portrayed really well, but she continued to live in that victim mentality with regular woe-is-me pity parties. Considering she got away from her abuser at 8, and she was 28, with a lot of counseling and loving foster parents in the last 20 years, sh</span>
  <span id="freeText14297348611996077394" style="display:none">On the one hand, I like the world that is building in these books. It is extremely intriguing and different.<br><br>On the other hand, I didn't particularly like the female love interest in this book - Tally. She was a victim of childhood abuse, and that was portrayed really well, but she continued to live in that victim mentality with regular woe-is-me pity parties. Considering she got away from her abuser at 8, and she was 28, with a lot of counseling and loving foster parents in the last 20 years, she sure seemed to resist the healing that they offered. And, along with being very self-pitying, she would also be combative with the person who was trying to help her. It didn't make sense, really.<br><br>At the beginning of the story, Tally was so afraid of Clay that she was paralyzed by fear. And yet, she then started baiting him. If she was so afraid of him, why would she actively try to get him angry? It just seemed weird. Hadn't she ever heard the saying, "Don't poke the bear?"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443590163i/16382591.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>and then have a refreshing drink of your own urine...</i><br><br>So, this was my least favorite book because of my dislike of Tally. But, I still love the world and am looking forward to Dorian's story in the next book.</span>

<div id="review_49873226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49873226" />
    <a title="Mojca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1359426-mojca"><img alt="Mojca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379576265p2/1359426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49873226?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mojca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mojca" href="/user/show/1359426-mojca">Mojca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=nalini-singh">nalini-singh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=bodyguard-military-merc-gov-cop-spy">bodyguard-military-merc-gov-cop-spy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=sci-fi-futuristic-fantasy">sci-fi-futuristic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=paranormal-romance-fantasy">paranormal-romance-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=shape-shifters">shape-shifters</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49873226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16084330170747336333">When I read the blurb before starting this book I was absolutely ecstatic. I was about to learn everything there is to learn about Clay, the guy that's intrigued me since book one....When I opened it and started reading I couldn't wait to get to the "good stuff"....Then after a few pages, my enthusiasm completely blanked out.<br/>Not because of Clay, of course, he's wonderful (as all changeling men are), though a bit too much on the wild side sometimes, and he could've pulled back on the whole "let's</span>
  <span id="freeText16084330170747336333" style="display:none">When I read the blurb before starting this book I was absolutely ecstatic. I was about to learn everything there is to learn about Clay, the guy that's intrigued me since book one....When I opened it and started reading I couldn't wait to get to the "good stuff"....Then after a few pages, my enthusiasm completely blanked out.<br />Not because of Clay, of course, he's wonderful (as all changeling men are), though a bit too much on the wild side sometimes, and he could've pulled back on the whole "let's blame the girl for the sins she committed" or cut it a little short instead of wallowing in <i>jealous rage</i> (as he put it) until it's almost too late.<br /><br />Nah, my enthusiasm died solely and because of the woman Ms. Singh decided to pair Clay with.<br />After three books with three strong female characters (two Psy and one changeling) and three incredible, drop-dead gorgeous and to-die-for male characters (two changeling and one Psy), we got one incredible, drop-dead gorgeous, to-die-for changeling that's dangerous to boot and a human. Which wouldn't be so bad, I'm human, we're all human, we root for human women to get one of these (see above) guys. Yet why the heck did Clay have to get the most obnoxious and hate-able female out there? After the three previous "gems" he's suddenly saddled with a terrified, spineless, often brainless, defective, self-punishing, emotional cripple of a woman. I never thought I'd say this but I really wished someone would just make her a snack and get a replacement female lead.<br />This is pure discrimination, people! Why should Psy and changeling women be so wonderful and this human bitch such a...Well, bitch?!<br />Not even the constant mentioning of her apparently fatal disease couldn't sway me. Hell, I wanted her dead. The continuous "emotional tennis match" in her head gave me the hives.<br />But something extraordinary happened (around page 200 if I'm not mistaken). She suddenly woke up a completely different person (and here I thought personality transplantations weren't possible), and I ended up quite liking the girl. After she finally decided that "ugly sex" won't ruin her "friendship" with Clay she grew up a spine, went shopping for a sense of humor, and became a completely different woman.<br /><br />I really didn't get the children-disappearing plot until the finishing revelation, and now I can't shake the nasty feeling the "evil doings" are starting to repeat. I like this series too much to see it get villains and deeds carbon copied from the previous one.<br />The only good thing this one brought was the introduction to a character that'll play a major role in the next book. I've already read the blurb and I waited with batted breath for the "meeting"...And after it wasn't only Talin that noticed something "strange".<br /><br />And I truly hope Councilor Kaleb Krychek ends up being a good guy. Or if not necessarily a <i>good</i> guy at least good enough to warrant his own book, because...<i>dressed only in a pair of loose black pants, his body covered with sweat</i>...is totally worth reading about. I wonder what he was doing. ;P</span>
  <a data-text-id="16084330170747336333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_386120728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386120728" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer7798761567649523486">I read this book years ago, but after just re-reading it for probably the 10th time I realized I had never reviewed it. This is one of my favorites in a series of favorites. I LOVE Clay and I loved Tally, and their connection is outstanding. I love that they have been connected since childhood and how that plays out into their adulthood. I can't gush enough about this book and series.</span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nalini Singh fans and paranormal romance fans</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer124825733&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124825733" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5228826414952885537">I have no idea why it took me this long to discover this series! I am such an idiot to have not found this sooner! Singh’s Psy-Changeling gets better and better with each book and I am seriously at a loss for words!<br/><br/>First off, <b>Talin</b> is my FAVOURITE HEROINE IN THE SERIES! I absolutely adore her! She’s a human, but she has as much bite as the other Psy girls and Brenna. Her past is a dark one and it has haunted her to this day. I will admit, I did tear up as I read some of the things that happened </span>
  <span id="freeText5228826414952885537" style="display:none">I have no idea why it took me this long to discover this series! I am such an idiot to have not found this sooner! Singh’s Psy-Changeling gets better and better with each book and I am seriously at a loss for words!<br /><br />First off, <b>Talin</b> is my FAVOURITE HEROINE IN THE SERIES! I absolutely adore her! She’s a human, but she has as much bite as the other Psy girls and Brenna. Her past is a dark one and it has haunted her to this day. I will admit, I did tear up as I read some of the things that happened to her. I loved the fact that Talin and Clay were childhood friends. It shows the depth of their relationship and Clay’s actions to protect her make a great basis for a blooming romance.<br /><br />I will admit, I didn’t like <b>Clay</b> in <i> Visions of Heat</i>. He was a total asshole to Faith, but we see why in this book. She reminded him of Tally and how they parted on bad terms. Although he is still the brooding kind of guy, I loved his playful side and seriously fell in love with him just as Talin did. Together, Clay and Talin are my favourite couple so far!<br /><br />The introduction of <b> Max Shannon </b> was great and I’m really looking forward to reading more about his character! Also, I can already tell that something is going to happen with <b>Aleine and Dorian</b>, am I right? I already like her. The fact that she gave up Jon and Noor shows that she’s got a heart. But WHY DO THEY ALWAYS HAVE TO GO FOR THE CHILDREN!? That infuriates me like nothing else!<br /><br />When I found out that Tally was dying, my heart broke. Hasn’t she endured enough? Yet she was still strong and managed to keep herself together for Jon’s sake. At the end, they found a “cure” and I just kept thinking that no one else deserved to live more than Tally. Her life has been a mess, but with Clay, she has found another chance at life.<br /><br />Nalini writes beautifully and already I am dying for the next book! Bring it on, Dorian! <br /><br />Favourite Quote:<br />She smiled, patted his arm. “Oh, Clay darling, if you had told me you were feeling irritated because your...problems, I wouldn’t have made a fuss.” She knew very well the changelings around her could hear every whispered word.<br />“Tally,” It was a warning growl.<br />“I mean it must be embarrassing for you...being that you’re such a big man.” Her tone implied all sorts of things. “Last night was an aberration, I’m sure. And if not, there are always the pills.”<br />Gasps sounded up and down the corridor.<br />Clay’s eyes blazed hot. “I’m going to show you aberration, you brat.” He turned and glared at their audience, as if memorizing every single face. <br />Suddenly, everyone had somewhere else to be. Only when he’d intimidated the corridor clear did he turn back to her. “I bet you think you’re funny.”<br />She grinned. “Yep.”<br />“I hope you still think that when I’m proving to you just how big I am.”<br />Her eyes dropped involuntarily to his pants and she realized she might have pushed him a tad too far.<br />“Now, Clay...”<br />Pressing his body against hers, he hugged her to him with one arm and bent to speak with his lips against her ear. “Now, Tally,” he mimicked.<br />“Bully.”<br />“Brat.”<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9963766983153079154">I am currently rereading this whole series, but I unfortunately had to DNF this one… and on page 21 no less… I know what you might think, so let me explain… this series as a whole is one of my all time favourites… but even when I read them originally quite a few years ago, I remembered this one as my least favourite and my vast dislike for Talin as the heroine… and I was very vividly reminded about all those feelings when I read the first two chapters (18 pages) so I decided to take a short brea</span>
  <span id="freeText9963766983153079154" style="display:none">I am currently rereading this whole series, but I unfortunately had to DNF this one… and on page 21 no less… I know what you might think, so let me explain… this series as a whole is one of my all time favourites… but even when I read them originally quite a few years ago, I remembered this one as my least favourite and my vast dislike for Talin as the heroine… and I was very vividly reminded about all those feelings when I read the first two chapters (18 pages) so I decided to take a short break from it… cause I was very determined not to skip any book… I figured I can always skim through some parts of certain books if I really don’t like them… but days has been passing me by and I had no urge to pick it back up… not even a little bit… and then my sister started to convince me to just DNF it if it bothers me that much… why should I read a book I so clearly do not enjoy? after I finally picked it back up and read those few additional pages I realized… why indeed? the majority time I read, it’s for pleasure (aside from few exceptions when I want to educate myself) so why the hell would I continue to read a book that makes me mad as fuck? I decided it’s a valid point and promptly decided to DNF it :) so yep, I am giving it 2 stars even though I reread this time only 21 pages, but it’s just… really not my cup of tea… I remember enough details about the main characters and how their romance goes to know that 2 stars are generous and if I would push through and force myself to actually read it, it might be even lower… if you love this book, I’m really happy for you :) but I am moving on to later installments :)<br /><br />XOXO<br /><br />A</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=genre-romance-interracial">genre-romance-interracial</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246093126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10721526770612908082"><i>Napa Valley, California</i><br/><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>★★★★☆ (This is a review of the audiobook.) Sometimes I think listeners of audiobooks have a distinct advantage over readers of hardcopy. If they are well narrated and well directed, as this one is, they can bring to life what the author intended, as tone, inflection, and reaction between characters and how they dialogue is so vital. Such is the case in the fourth installment of Ms. Singh’s <i>Psy-changeling</i> series, which is read by <b>Angela Dawe</b>. She does an awesom</span>
  <span id="freeText10721526770612908082" style="display:none"><i>Napa Valley, California</i><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>★★★★☆ (This is a review of the audiobook.) Sometimes I think listeners of audiobooks have a distinct advantage over readers of hardcopy. If they are well narrated and well directed, as this one is, they can bring to life what the author intended, as tone, inflection, and reaction between characters and how they dialogue is so vital. Such is the case in the fourth installment of Ms. Singh’s <i>Psy-changeling</i> series, which is read by <b>Angela Dawe</b>. She does an awesome job on this one and it is no surprise she is a finalist this year for her narration in another audiobook (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10814693.The_Watch_That_Ends_the_Night_Voices_from_the_Titanic" title="The Watch That Ends the Night Voices from the Titanic by Allan Wolf" rel="nofollow noopener">The Watch That Ends the Night: Voices from the Titanic</a>) by the Audio Publishers Association’s: the prestigious <b>Audiobook of the Year and Distinguished Achievement in Production Award</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379769663i/280857.jpg" width="150" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12281064.Mine_to_Possess__Psy_Changeling___4_" title="Mine to Possess (Psy-Changeling, #4) by Nalini Singh" rel="nofollow noopener">Mine to Possess</a> Clay and Talin have a quite a past. He killed for her; she vomits at the mere thought of violence. He <i>is</i> violence personified; she faked her death to avoid him. Several readers are not too fond of Talin, the heroine in <i>Mine to Possess</i>, and think she owed Clay a little more groveling time. Be aware, I tend to sympathize with my heroines more than other readers, so I found my heart breaking over Talin’s abusive past. For me, these are <i>
  <b>two equally tortured individuals</b>
</i> who separate and come together again through violence. I like seeing Clay and Talin recalling their former childhood relationship, while warily getting to know each other as adults. That said, I must admit that by more than half way through I was ready to jump into the pages of this one and straighten these two protagonists out. Enough flip-flopping, suspicion, and self-doubt already!<br><br>Still, Ms. Singh is an excellent writer. I love the way she can turn a phrase to make me gasp, hold my breath, cringe, laugh, and sigh. She knows her characters and lets us get to know them. Others individuals – from past and future books – are presented seamlessly into the storyline, not just thrown in to appease fans. You want to know what makes her wicked evildoers tick and her ferocious heroes protect. Her world building is convincing, intriguing, and – more important – <b>consistent</b>. Her sensual scenes have a palpable chemistry that is there because she sets up her characters so perfectly. Plus, she is great at creating a sense of foreboding; while each installment in this series gives us a little satisfaction, it dishes out a little more dark mystery that is an integral part of her magical Psy-Changeling World.<br><br><i>Psy-Changeling Audiobook Covers</i><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10832348.Slave_to_Sensation" title="Slave to Sensation by Nalini Singh" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1303766887s/10832348.jpg" alt="Slave to Sensation by Nalini Singh" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10833626.Visions_of_Heat" title="Visions of Heat by Nalini Singh" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10833665.Caressed_by_Ice" title="Caressed by Ice by Nalini Singh" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer1199591500450423561">5 stars – Paranormal Romance<br/><br/>This is yet another terrific read and a beautiful romance in the intriguing <i>Psy-Changeling</i> universe and my second favorite of the series so far. I wondered if/how Singh could possibly top <b>Caressed by Ice</b>, and while that’s still my favorite, this one isn’t that far behind and the series just keeps getting better and better. The writing is superb, the characters are fascinating, well developed, and rich, the world building is captivating, and the romance is emotional, i</span>
  <span id="freeText1199591500450423561" style="display:none">5 stars – Paranormal Romance<br /><br />This is yet another terrific read and a beautiful romance in the intriguing <i>Psy-Changeling</i> universe and my second favorite of the series so far. I wondered if/how Singh could possibly top <b>Caressed by Ice</b>, and while that’s still my favorite, this one isn’t that far behind and the series just keeps getting better and better. The writing is superb, the characters are fascinating, well developed, and rich, the world building is captivating, and the romance is emotional, intense, and passionate.<br /><br />This time around, the spotlight is on Changeling DarkRiver sentinel leopard Clay Bennett and his former childhood mate, human Talin McKade. An extreme act of violence years ago drove Clay and Tally apart, but now children are disappearing from the shelter where Tally is a social-worker and she’s determined to enlist Clay’s help. Clay and Tally have both experienced more sorrow, violence, bloodshed, and loss than anyone should ever have to endure and it’s scarred them both. Now that fate has finally brought them back together, can they finally heal from the pain of the past and find a way to be mates, forever? <br /><br />Singh really knows how to write broken, emotionally battered characters that find healing, peace, and love through bonds with the destined mates of their hearts/souls, and <b>Mine to Possess</b> is another winner with that same theme. The romance between Clay and Tally is an emotional rollercoaster full of deep passion and it tugs the heartstrings. It’s another fabulous read in an extraordinary, top-notch paranormal, sci-fi/fantasy romance series. 5 stars!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3653734938729538385"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417997437i/12633821.png' width='400' height='169' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What an amazing book, as usual. <div id="review_156612940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156612940" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4926376-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317086742p2/4926376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156612940?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/4926376-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jessica by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1600566-calisto">Calisto</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer156612940&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156612940" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer28371145698135407">The background plot was the only thing that saved this book. I had no patience for the heroine despite the fact that the author attempts to give her a background that will not only explain the character's actions and the way she treats others, but also tries to paint her in a sympathetic light. For me, it failed completely. <br/><br/>Psychologically, I can understand the attempt by the author to choose to make Talin, the heroine, act the way she does because of her past. And by act the way she does, I mea</span>
  <span id="freeText28371145698135407" style="display:none">The background plot was the only thing that saved this book. I had no patience for the heroine despite the fact that the author attempts to give her a background that will not only explain the character's actions and the way she treats others, but also tries to paint her in a sympathetic light. For me, it failed completely. <br /><br />Psychologically, I can understand the attempt by the author to choose to make Talin, the heroine, act the way she does because of her past. And by act the way she does, I mean that Talin holds herself at a distance and has a hard time trusting others, which, again, I can understand taking the approach of past childhood abuse. However, the rest of her personality, the manipulative, self-centered, and combative part, makes the reader distance themselves from the character and begin to wonder why they should even care about a happily ever after for dear Talin. Additionally, I found the interaction and dialogue between Talin and Clay to be the weakest of the series, but part of that could be due to my severe disinterest in Talin. <br /><br />As I said before, the background plot was what kept me going in this book. That and the promise that there were other, better, books to be read in the series once I crawled my way through Talin and her manipulative ways. You could start to feel all the threads being put in place in the previous book by Nalini Singh, but Mine to Possess is where you can start to see them weave together to help create a fuller and more intriguing world. I look forward to seeing what she does with this universe but please, for all that I can beg, please don't make me suffer through more of Talin. I'm not sure I can do it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="28371145698135407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17782561387258641098" style="display:none">Ok, this has become my new favorite in the series so far. Clay and Talin had me from the very beginning and I couldn’t put this down. <br /><br />At first they are both kind of cruel to each other. Clay lashing out because of how she hurt him, and Talin because of the trauma she suffered as a child. She comes off pretty weak in the beginning, but the more time she spends with Clay, the stronger she gets.<br /><br />Despite his anger with her, Clay was very protective and possessive. I wanted to shake Talin for not getting past her fear and insecurities sooner. You could just tell Clay would be good to her because of how much he loved her, and he does prove that.<br /><br />This will be the couple to beat in the upcoming books.</span>

They met as children and they had a beautiful friendship. I loved the insight to them and their friendship when they were children. Even back then they were destined to be mates. <br /><br />“Clay, if anyone followed anyone, it was me tagging along after you. I didn’t dare order you around.”<br /><br />“Load of shit,” he muttered, but she thought she heard a softening in his tone. “You fucking made me attend tea parties.”<br /><br />She remembered his threat before the first one: “Tell anyone and I’ll eat you and use your bones as toothpicks.”<br /><br />Then one fateful night everything changed they were ripped apart in the most horrible way. Clay wanted to protect Tally. <br /><br />Did I want to like Clay? No. Did I like him? She was scared and mad, he sacrificed so much for her and she was being a brat about it. All in all she was an okay heroine, Clay really made up for it but he was being a mean bastard and he was cruel but he was hurt. <br /><br />Tally works for the Shine Foundation they take in gifted children and give them a future, slight problem, children are being kidnapped and found dead. As Tally works for the foundation and one of her kids is missing she goes to Clay for help. He ends up helping her. <br /><br />They work their differences out and they have a unique bond like no other. <br /><br />Any resistance she might’ve harbored to this dangerous, inevitable escalation in their relationship dissolved into a big fat pool at her feet. He was being charming. Clay did not do charm, not for anyone. Except, it seemed, her. She pressed a kiss to his jaw. “Stop being so sexy.”<br /><br />Through their strong need to protect one another they pushed each other away. And when they are open with one another? And trust one another? Then it is beautiful.<br /><br />Undeniably, irrevocably his. No matter what she thought or how she’s run from him. Talin had always been, and would always be, his. –Clay-<br /><br />The man he had grown into – well he enchanted her, brooding temper, dark kisses, animal protectiveness, and all. -Talin-<br /><br />Not cool Faith, not cool. I liked you, well I still do and she did apologize. <br /><br />This book was like a chess game, played by the most talented chess players out there. All the pieces came together nicely and none of it was predictable. <br /><br />Protocol I is having problems as is the council. The weakening of the PsyNet and the sociopaths and psychopaths is getting worse as those feelings have been repressed for a long time, everything is about to crumble. Then there are the Forgotten, brilliant!<br /><br />The Web of Stars was now feed by the thoughts and dreams of all races. Their world was a triumvirate, and for the first time in a hundred years that triumvirate was complete on a psychic level.</b></span>

    <a title="Steven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11855472-steven"><img alt="Steven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541604404p2/11855472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2289207990?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven" href="/user/show/11855472-steven">Steven</a>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8750613693276776808"><b> A very good addition to the Psy/Changeling series, Mine to Possess was a great read that just underlined this series as one of the best in my "read" list <a href='http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&current=167153.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/361833.gif' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a> </b><br/><br/>Clay and Tally knew each other since they were kids, and their bond was created through friendship, and later through Clay's act of protectiveness, him killing her foster father and saving her from further abuse and eventually death by the sick idiot.<br/>Tally witnessed the murder and was mentally scarred by it, and eventually became terrified by</span>
  <span id="freeText8750613693276776808" style="display:none"><b> A very good addition to the Psy/Changeling series, Mine to Possess was a great read that just underlined this series as one of the best in my "read" list <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=167153.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/361833.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </b><br><br>Clay and Tally knew each other since they were kids, and their bond was created through friendship, and later through Clay's act of protectiveness, him killing her foster father and saving her from further abuse and eventually death by the sick idiot.<br>Tally witnessed the murder and was mentally scarred by it, and eventually became terrified by Clay himself.<br>After 20 years, Clay thinks Tally's dead, untill one night she appears and asks him a favour.<br><br>Their relationship was difficult from the start, Tally was terrified of him, and he was furious because of that. Even though Clay knew they were meant to be together, he still couldn't forgive her for faking her death and making him believe she was dead for so many years. Tally was still affraid of him, but most of all, she couldn't forgive him for leaving her alone after that terrible night (he went to jail) so they were up and down then down and up all the time XDXD <br><br>The story was good, like always, love the world the author created, even the bad guys are interesting and I love reading their plots and how it all ends :) <br><br>4 stars all in all, it was just that something was missing in their relationship, the constant "does he love me, we can't be together, did she forgive me, did he forgive me, why aren't we mated, I want to be mated, we're mated but she doesn't know it" and stuff like that <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=798186.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380222758i/362515.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=shame.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372925ra/726353.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The subplot in this one was about Ashaya Aleine <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=bliss.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/357951.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> it got me hooked, looks like her book is going to be great <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=963779.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755356346?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica Ravenclaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica Ravenclaw" href="/user/show/12099580-erica-ravenclaw">Erica Ravenclaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755356346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17160927053334973498">Can we all talk about this cover for a moment? Let's look at it together shall we?<br/><br/><a href='http://s1212.photobucket.com/user/PetiteAme/media/Halloween%20Upload/GIFS/1830755_zpsc2daf0fe.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383452638i/6564038.jpg' alt=' photo 1830755_zpsc2daf0fe.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>There it is...unapologetically shoving it's fabulousness in your face. Leopard spotted male dashing through... fire? Oh and this font, YES THIS FONT. I'm an absolute judge a book by it's cover person, and this magnificent piece of art screams LITE ME ON FIRE I AM TERRIBLE. <br/><br/>I don't have anything good to say about this book, it was my least favorite thus far in the series. First of all the male lead's name is Cla</span>
  <span id="freeText17160927053334973498" style="display:none">Can we all talk about this cover for a moment? Let's look at it together shall we?<br><br><a href="http://s1212.photobucket.com/user/PetiteAme/media/Halloween%20Upload/GIFS/1830755_zpsc2daf0fe.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383452638i/6564038.jpg" alt=" photo 1830755_zpsc2daf0fe.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There it is...unapologetically shoving it's fabulousness in your face. Leopard spotted male dashing through... fire? Oh and this font, YES THIS FONT. I'm an absolute judge a book by it's cover person, and this magnificent piece of art screams LITE ME ON FIRE I AM TERRIBLE. <br><br>I don't have anything good to say about this book, it was my least favorite thus far in the series. First of all the male lead's name is Clay and really all I can see is Clay from SoA talking about lapping his mate "straight up". Jesus H Clay, stop talking about cream while you are going down on her. It's giving me the fucking creeps. The female lead is extremely unlikeable, and a whole lot of "can't talk about this or you won't like me anymore" plot lines. Truthfully, that feels like lying and I'm just not one of those people, I found it nearly impossible to relate and a tad skeevy. <br><br>There is one redeeming quality that I was very surprised about, this is the first book in this genre (that I have read) that has addressed the scars of childhood sexual abuse in adulthood, I was impressed such a dark subject matter was discussed openly. It also went on to follow her stages of healing and what sexual and intimate relationships are supposed to look like. <br><br>Onward. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17160927053334973498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_62429492" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62429492" />
    <a title="valee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2320890-valee"><img alt="valee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443365004p2/2320890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62429492?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="valee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="valee" href="/user/show/2320890-valee">valee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575100008" href="/book/show/8711617-mine-to-possess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2320890-valee?shelf=amazing-pnr-romance">amazing-pnr-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62429492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13663314454334241415">I never thought I would be saying this but this is definitely a series that <b>REQUIRES a RE-READ!</b> I'm so happy I read this book again, things are so different for me now. First time I rated it with 4 stars, but this time that I was aware how things would be and I already knew the new characters introduced in it, I was able to understand everything better. I realized this is a far more complex series that I thought it was and that without a re-read you are not really able to fully comprehend it. Ev</span>
  <span id="freeText13663314454334241415" style="display:none">I never thought I would be saying this but this is definitely a series that <b>REQUIRES a RE-READ!</b> I'm so happy I read this book again, things are so different for me now. First time I rated it with 4 stars, but this time that I was aware how things would be and I already knew the new characters introduced in it, I was able to understand everything better. I realized this is a far more complex series that I thought it was and that without a re-read you are not really able to fully comprehend it. Everything is crystal clear to me now, I understand so many things I just skimmed the first time I read it...<br /><br />In this instalment we get to read about Clay. We didn't know much about him from the previous books, just that he was a very dangerous enemy to have, a powerful sentinel and a lethal adversary; but we didn't know a thing about his past or childhood. Well, in this book we get to fully know him. Clay is half leopard, half human, although his DNA is fully leopard. He was raised between humans, which was something really interesting to read about as we get to see how his animal reacts while he is growing and doesn't have what it needs to be content. We are also introduce to his heroine while he remembers the past. Tally was his childhood sweetheart, the only person who could fully accept him and comprehend him. But both of them were raised in a terrible environment. Not only was she abused and violated in every way by the people who should have protected her but she was needing something she wasn't aware she needed nor what it was. All this got to break her, to make her chose a path that got her away from Clay.<br /><br />But many years later they got to reunite. And I loved to read about this for a second time because it made me change fully my POV about Tally. The first time I read this book I didn't like her, I thought she was a weak heroine and just not what Clay needed at all. I just realized I was terribly wrong. Tally was one of the most strong heroines I have read about in this series. She was strong enough to stay sane after everything that happened to her, and she was able to defend herself even though she was human. I love Tally now, which is weird because I remember hating her the first read I did. I guess that this time, as I knew what type of heroine she would be, I got to appreciate other details better.<br /><br />To sum up I just wanted to insist that <b> everybody should make a re-read of this series</b>, really. Things are so different after you read it once and have an idea of things you didn't the first time. I did my first read 2 years ago so things were not very clear on my mind. I had forgotten many things and it was amazing to remember everything all over again. <b> As this is such a complex series, with many characters and paranormal background information, it's a huge help to do this re-read. This 2nd time I felt I already knew all the characters, so I never got mixed up with names or what their role was going to be. This way, I was able to focus on the really important stuff. </b><br /><br />I LOVE THIS SERIES! I'm just getting ready for Hawke's book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13663314454334241415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18381584787352699359">I love this story. The fact Talin is human only makes it even more extraordinary. It's easier to make changelings and Psy intriguing. <br/>***<br/>There could be spoilers here. <br/><br/>This is one of those books people either hate or love. <br/><br/>Some people seem to hate Talin.   <span id="freeText18381584787352699359" style="display:none">I love this story. The fact Talin is human only makes it even more extraordinary. It's easier to make changelings and Psy intriguing. <br />***<br />There could be spoilers here. <br /><br />This is one of those books people either hate or love. <br /><br />Some people seem to hate Talin. They see her as weak. It seems to them that she betrayed Clay because she hid from him, let him think she is dead. Now she needs help and Clay is the one to do it.<br /><br />I kind of understand the frustration. I see their point. Me, I don't see Talin like that. She was sexually abused when she was only a toddler and it continued till she was eight. The guy was her foster parent and a serial killer. Clay was the one to kill him. The state took her away, placed her with a nice family and she let Clay think she is dead.<br />I've read quite a few comments saying she betrayed him and each and every one are written as if they are referring to a freaking adult. She was eight years old! The moment Clay realises just how much pain she is in is one of the most heartbreaking moments I've ever read.<br />So, yes, I do feel sorry for him for being left behind. Everyone seems to forget a very important detail that Talin did not tell the authorities that the abuser begged Clay for his life. That 'tiny' detail would have landed Clay in more trouble. Such as they were, Clay's actions were seen as a defence.<br /><br />Talin is back and she pretty much annoys a lot of readers with her behaviour. I see it as a coping mechanism. She is the one who is alone now. <br /><br />I love that finally this is about a human-changeling relationship. I see Talin as strong even with her flaws. You do not get over the things you have seen and experienced and act as if nothing happened.</span>
